<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1000_Potiomkin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="735" data-file-width="496" decoding="async" height="356" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/1000_Potiomkin.jpg/240px-1000_Potiomkin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/1000_Potiomkin.jpg/360px-1000_Potiomkin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/1000_Potiomkin.jpg/480px-1000_Potiomkin.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1000_Potiomkin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Catherine II and <a href="/wiki/Grigory_Potemkin" title="Grigory Potemkin">Potemkin</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_of_Russia" title="Millennium of Russia">Millennium Monument</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Novgorod" title="Novgorod">Novgorod</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Grigory_Potemkin" title="Grigory Potemkin">Grigory Potemkin</a> was involved in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palace_coup" title="Palace coup">palace coup</a></i> of 1762. In 1772, Catherine's close friends informed her of Orlov's affairs with other women, and she dismissed him. By the winter of 1773, the <a href="/wiki/Pugachev%27s_Rebellion" title="Pugachev's Rebellion">Pugachev revolt</a> had started to threaten. Catherine's son Paul had started gaining support; both of these trends threatened her power. She called Potemkin for help – mostly military – and he became devoted to her.
</p><p>In 1772, Catherine wrote to Potemkin. Days earlier, she had found out about an uprising in the Volga region. She appointed General <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Bibikov" title="Aleksandr Bibikov">Aleksandr Bibikov</a> to put down the uprising, but she needed Potemkin's advice on military strategy. Potemkin quickly gained positions and awards. Russian poets wrote about his virtues, the court praised him, foreign ambassadors fought for his favour, and his family moved into the palace. He later became the de facto absolute ruler of New Russia, governing its colonisation.
</p><p>In 1780, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph II, Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor Joseph II</a>, the son of Holy Roman Empress Maria Theresa, toyed with the idea of determining whether or not to enter an alliance with Russia, and asked to meet Catherine. Potemkin had the task of briefing him and travelling with him to Saint Petersburg. Potemkin also convinced Catherine to expand the universities in Russia to increase the number of scientists.
</p><p>Catherine was worried that Potemkin's poor health would delay his important work in colonising and developing the south as he had planned. He died at the age of 52 in 1791.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_months_and_death">Final months and death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Final months and death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catherine_II_walking_by_V.Borovikovskiy_(1794,_Tretyakov_gallery).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="1350" decoding="async" height="356" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Catherine_II_walking_by_V.Borovikovskiy_%281794%2C_Tretyakov_gallery%29.jpg/240px-Catherine_II_walking_by_V.Borovikovskiy_%281794%2C_Tretyakov_gallery%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Catherine_II_walking_by_V.Borovikovskiy_%281794%2C_Tretyakov_gallery%29.jpg/360px-Catherine_II_walking_by_V.Borovikovskiy_%281794%2C_Tretyakov_gallery%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Catherine_II_walking_by_V.Borovikovskiy_%281794%2C_Tretyakov_gallery%29.jpg/480px-Catherine_II_walking_by_V.Borovikovskiy_%281794%2C_Tretyakov_gallery%29.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Catherine_II_walking_by_V.Borovikovskiy_(1794,_Tretyakov_gallery).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1794 portrait of Catherine, aged approximately 65, with the <a href="/wiki/Chesme_Column" title="Chesme Column">Chesme Column</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Park" title="Catherine Park">Catherine Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tsarskoye_Selo" title="Tsarskoye Selo">Tsarskoye Selo</a> in the background</div></div></div>
<p>Though Catherine's life and reign included remarkable personal successes, they ended in two failures. Her Swedish cousin (once removed), King <a href="/wiki/Gustav_IV_Adolf" title="Gustav IV Adolf">Gustav IV Adolf</a>, visited her in September 1796, the empress's intention being that her granddaughter Alexandra should become queen of Sweden by marriage. A ball was given at the imperial court on 11 September when the engagement was supposed to be announced. Gustav Adolph felt pressured to accept that Alexandra would not convert to <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a>, and though he was delighted by the young lady, he refused to appear at the ball and left for Stockholm. The frustration affected Catherine's health. She recovered well enough to begin to plan a ceremony which would establish her favourite grandson <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Alexander</a> as her heir, superseding her difficult son Paul, but she died before the announcement could be made, just over two months after the engagement ball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grande_p._427_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grande_p._427-136">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 16 November [<a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">O.S.</a> 5 November] 1796, Catherine rose early in the morning and had her usual morning coffee, soon settling down to work on papers; she told her lady's maid, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Perekusikhina" title="Maria Perekusikhina">Maria Perekusikhina</a>, that she had slept better than she had in a long time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rounding,_p._499_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rounding,_p._499-137">[133]</a></sup> Sometime after 9:00 she was found on the floor with her face purplish, her pulse weak, her breathing shallow and laboured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rounding,_p._499_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rounding,_p._499-137">[133]</a></sup> The court physician diagnosed a <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">stroke</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rounding,_p._499_137-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rounding,_p._499-137">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dixon,_p._315_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dixon,_p._315-138">[134]</a></sup> and despite attempts to revive her she fell into a coma. She was given the <a href="/wiki/Last_rites" title="Last rites">last rites</a> and died the following evening around 9:45.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dixon,_p._315_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dixon,_p._315-138">[134]</a></sup> An autopsy confirmed a stroke as the cause of death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[135]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Platon_Zubov_by_Eggink.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1134" data-file-width="892" decoding="async" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Platon_Zubov_by_Eggink.jpg/170px-Platon_Zubov_by_Eggink.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Platon_Zubov_by_Eggink.jpg/255px-Platon_Zubov_by_Eggink.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Platon_Zubov_by_Eggink.jpg/340px-Platon_Zubov_by_Eggink.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Platon_Zubov_by_Eggink.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Catherine's last favourite, <a href="/wiki/Platon_Zubov" title="Platon Zubov">Platon Zubov</a></div></div></div>
<p>Later, <a href="/wiki/Legends_of_Catherine_the_Great#Death_narratives" title="Legends of Catherine the Great">several rumors</a> circulated regarding the cause and manner of her death. The most famous of these rumors is that she died after having sex with her horse. This rumor was widely circulated by satirical British and French publications at the time of her death. In his 1647 book <i>Beschreibung der muscowitischen und persischen Reise</i> (<i>Description of the Muscovite and Persian journey</i>), German scholar <a href="/wiki/Adam_Olearius" title="Adam Olearius">Adam Olearius</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-r508_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-r508-140">[136]</a></sup> Olearius's claims about a supposed Russian tendency towards <a href="/wiki/Zoophilia" title="Zoophilia">bestiality</a> with horses was often repeated in anti-Russian literature throughout the 17th and 18th centuries to illustrate the alleged barbarous "Asian" nature of Russia. Given the frequency which this story was repeated together with Catherine's love of her adopted homeland and her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hippophilia" title="Hippophilia">hippophilia</a>, it is likely that these details were conflated into this rumor. Catherine had been targeted for being an unmarried.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[137]</a></sup>
</p><p>Catherine's undated will, discovered in early 1792 among her papers by her secretary Alexander Vasilievich Khrapovitsky, gave specific instructions should she die: "Lay out my corpse dressed in white, with a golden crown on my head, and on it inscribe my Christian name. Mourning dress is to be worn for six months, and no longer: the shorter the better."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[138]</a></sup> In the end, the empress was laid to rest with a gold crown on her head and clothed in a silver <a href="/wiki/Brocade" title="Brocade">brocade</a> dress. On 25 November, the coffin, richly decorated in gold fabric, was placed atop an elevated platform at the Grand Gallery's chamber of mourning, designed and decorated by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Rinaldi_(architect)" title="Antonio Rinaldi (architect)">Antonio Rinaldi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[140]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/%C3%89lisabeth_Vig%C3%A9e_Le_Brun" title="Élisabeth Vigée Le Brun">Élisabeth Vigée Le Brun</a>: "The empress's body lay in state for six weeks in a large and magnificently decorated room in the castle, which was kept lit day and night. Catherine was stretched on a ceremonial bed surrounded by the coats of arms of all the towns in Russia. Her face was left uncovered, and her fair hand rested on the bed. All the ladies, some of whom took turn to watch by the body, would go and kiss this hand, or at least appear to." A description of the empress's funeral is written in Madame Vigée Le Brun's memoirs.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Children">Children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td>Miscarriage
</td>
<td>20 December 1752
</td>
<td>According to court gossip, this lost pregnancy was attributed to <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Saltykov" title="Sergei Saltykov">Sergei Saltykov</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Troyat_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-Troyat-145">[141]</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Miscarriage
</td>
<td>30 June 1753
</td>
<td>This second lost pregnancy was also attributed to Saltykov;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Troyat_145-1"><a href="#cite_note-Troyat-145">[141]</a></sup> this time she was very ill for 13 days. Catherine later wrote in her memoirs: "...They suspect that part of the afterbirth has not come away ... on the 13th day it came out by itself".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[143]</a></sup>

<tr>
<td><b><a href="/wiki/Paul_I_of_Russia" title="Paul I of Russia">Paul (I) Petrovich</a></b><br/>Emperor of Russia
</td>
<td>1 October 1754 –<br/> 23 March 1801 (Age: 46)
</td>
<td>Born at the Winter Palace, officially he was a son of Peter III but in her memoirs, Catherine implies very strongly that Saltykov was the biological father of the child.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[144]</a></sup> He married firstly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natalia_Alexeievna_of_Russia" title="Natalia Alexeievna of Russia">Princess Wilhelmina Louisa of Hesse-Darmstadt</a> in 1773 and had no issue. He married secondly, in 1776, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Feodorovna_(Sophie_Dorothea_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg)" title="Maria Feodorovna (Sophie Dorothea of Württemberg)">Princess Sophie Dorothea of Württemberg</a> and had issue, including the future <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Alexander I of Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Russia" title="Nicholas I of Russia">Nicholas I of Russia</a>. He succeeded as emperor of Russia in 1796 and was murdered at <a href="/wiki/Saint_Michael%27s_Castle" title="Saint Michael's Castle">Saint Michael's Castle</a> in 1801.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Anna Petrovna<br/>Grand Duchess of Russia
</td>
<td>9 December 1757 –<br/> 8 March 1759 (Age: 15 months)
</td>
<td>Possibly the offspring of Catherine and Stanislaus Poniatowski, Anna was born at the Winter Palace between 10 and 11 o'clock;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[145]</a></sup> she was named by Empress Elizabeth after <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchess_Anna_Petrovna_of_Russia" title="Grand Duchess Anna Petrovna of Russia">her deceased sister</a>, against Catherine's wishes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-massie_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-massie-150">[146]</a></sup> On 17 December 1757, Anna was baptised and received the Great Cross of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_Catherine" title="Order of Saint Catherine">Order of Saint Catherine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[147]</a></sup> Elizabeth served as godmother; she held Anna above the baptismal font and brought Catherine, who did not witness any of the celebrations, and Peter a gift of 60,000 rubles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-massie_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-massie-150">[146]</a></sup> Elizabeth took Anna and raised the baby herself, as she had done with Paul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[148]</a></sup> In her memoirs, Catherine makes no mention of Anna's death on 8 March 1759,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[149]</a></sup> though she was inconsolable and entered a state of shock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[150]</a></sup> Anna's funeral took place on 15 March, at <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky_Lavra" title="Alexander Nevsky Lavra">Alexander Nevsky Lavra</a>. After the funeral, Catherine never mentioned her dead daughter again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAlexander1989[httpsarchiveorgdetailscatherinegreatli0000alexpage54_54]_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlexander1989[httpsarchiveorgdetailscatherinegreatli0000alexpage54_54]-155">[151]</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexei_Grigorievich_Bobrinsky" title="Alexei Grigorievich Bobrinsky">Alexei Grigorievich Bobrinsky</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%91%D0%BE%D0%B1%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9,_%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%93%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%8C%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87" title="ru:Бобринский, Алексей Григорьевич">ru</a>]</span></b><br/><a href="/wiki/Bobrinsky" title="Bobrinsky">Count Bobrinsky</a>
</td>
<td>11 April 1762 –<br/> 20 June 1813 (Age: 51)
</td>
<td>Born at the Winter Palace, he was brought up at <a href="/wiki/Novomoskovsk,_Russia" title="Novomoskovsk, Russia">Bobriki</a>; his father was Grigory Grigoryevich Orlov. He married Baroness Anna Dorothea von Ungern-Sternberg and had issue. Created Count Bobrinsky in 1796, he died in 1813.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Grigorieva_Temkina" title="Elizabeth Grigorieva Temkina">Elizabeth Grigorevna Temkina</a> (alleged daughter)
</td>
<td>13 July 1775 –<br/> 25 May 1854 (Age: 78)
</td>
<td>Born many years after the death of Catherine's husband, brought up in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samoilov" title="Samoilov">Samoilov</a> household as Grigory Potemkin's daughter, and never acknowledged by Catherine, it has been suggested that Temkina was the illegitimate child of Catherine and Potemkin, but this is now regarded as unlikely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Montefiore2010_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Montefiore2010-156">[152]</a></sup>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_descendants">Royal descendants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Royal descendants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The royal families of Britain, Denmark, Netherlands, Spain and Sweden descend from Catherine the Great, as well as the former royal families of Greece, Romania, Yugoslavia and many others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[153]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_royalty">British royalty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: British royalty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Olga_Constantinovna_of_Russia" title="Olga Constantinovna of Russia">Olga Constantinovna of Russia</a>, great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was the paternal grandmother of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh</a> and his descendants, including <a href="/wiki/Charles_III" title="Charles III">Charles III</a>, the King of the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland; his son, <a href="/wiki/William,_Prince_of_Wales" title="William, Prince of Wales">William, Prince of Wales</a>; and William's son, <a href="/wiki/Prince_George_of_Wales" title="Prince George of Wales">Prince George of Wales</a>.
</p><p>Also, she was a maternal ancestor of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Edward,_2nd_Duke_of_Kent" title="Prince Edward, 2nd Duke of Kent">Prince Edward, 2nd Duke of Kent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Princess_Alexandra,_The_Honourable_Lady_Ogilvy" title="Princess Alexandra, The Honourable Lady Ogilvy">Princess Alexandra, The Honourable Lady Ogilvy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Michael_of_Kent" title="Prince Michael of Kent">Prince Michael of Kent</a> in three ways through her descendant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Marina,_Duchess_of_Kent" title="Princess Marina, Duchess of Kent">Princess Marina, Duchess of Kent</a>:
</p>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elena_Pavlovna_of_Russia" title="Elena Pavlovna of Russia">Elena Pavlovna of Russia</a>, Grand Duchess of Mecklenburg-Schwerin, and granddaughter of Catherine, was a maternal great-great-great-great-grandmother of the three people mentioned above.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Olga_Constantinovna_of_Russia" title="Olga Constantinovna of Russia">Olga Constantinovna of Russia</a>, great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was a maternal great-grandmother of the three people mentioned above.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_Vladimir_Alexandrovich_of_Russia" title="Grand Duke Vladimir Alexandrovich of Russia">Grand Duke Vladimir Alexandrovich of Russia</a>, great-great-grandson of Catherine, was a maternal great-grandfather of the three people mentioned above.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Danish_royalty">Danish royalty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Danish royalty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elena_Pavlovna_of_Russia" title="Elena Pavlovna of Russia">Elena Pavlovna of Russia</a>, Grand Duchess of Mecklenburg-Schwerin, and granddaughter of Catherine, was a paternal great-great-great-great-grandmother of Queen <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_II_of_Denmark" title="Margrethe II of Denmark">Margrethe II of Denmark</a>.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anastasia_Mikhailovna_of_Russia" title="Anastasia Mikhailovna of Russia">Anastasia Mikhailovna of Russia</a>, Grand Duchess of Mecklenburg-Schwerin, and great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was a paternal great-grandmother of Queen <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_II_of_Denmark" title="Margrethe II of Denmark">Margrethe II of Denmark</a>.
</p><p>Also, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchess_Maria_Pavlovna_of_Russia_(1786%E2%80%931859)" title="Grand Duchess Maria Pavlovna of Russia (1786–1859)">Grand Duchess Maria Pavlovna of Russia</a>, was a granddaughter of Catherine, and great-great-great-grandmother of <a href="/wiki/Victoria_of_Baden" title="Victoria of Baden">Victoria of Baden</a>, who was a maternal great-grandmother of Queen <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_II_of_Denmark" title="Margrethe II of Denmark">Margrethe II of Denmark</a>.
</p><p>Furthermore, the Grand Duchess Maria Pavlovna of Russia was also the great-great-great-grandmother of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louise_Margaret_of_Prussia" title="Louise Margaret of Prussia">Louise Margaret of Prussia</a>, who was another maternal great-grandmother of Queen <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_II_of_Denmark" title="Margrethe II of Denmark">Margrethe II of Denmark</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_royalty">Dutch royalty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Dutch royalty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elena_Pavlovna_of_Russia" title="Elena Pavlovna of Russia">Elena Pavlovna of Russia</a>, Grand Duchess of Mecklenburg-Schwerin, and granddaughter of Catherine, was the paternal great-great-grandmother of Queen <a href="/wiki/Juliana_of_the_Netherlands" title="Juliana of the Netherlands">Juliana of the Netherlands</a>, who was the maternal grandmother of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Willem-Alexander_of_the_Netherlands" title="King Willem-Alexander of the Netherlands">King Willem-Alexander of the Netherlands</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Anna_Pavlovna_of_Russia" title="Anna Pavlovna of Russia">Anna Pavlovna of Russia</a>, granddaughter of Catherine, was maternal great-grandmother of Queen <a href="/wiki/Juliana_of_the_Netherlands" title="Juliana of the Netherlands">Juliana of the Netherlands</a>, who was the maternal grandmother of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Willem-Alexander_of_the_Netherlands" title="King Willem-Alexander of the Netherlands">King Willem-Alexander of the Netherlands</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_royalty">Spanish royalty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Spanish royalty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Olga_Constantinovna_of_Russia" title="Olga Constantinovna of Russia">Olga Constantinovna of Russia</a>, great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was the maternal great-great-grandmother of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Felipe_VI" title="King Felipe VI">King Felipe VI</a>.
</p><p>Also, <a href="/wiki/Sophia_of_Prussia" title="Sophia of Prussia">Sophia of Prussia</a>, great-great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was a maternal great-grandmother of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Felipe_VI" title="King Felipe VI">King Felipe VI</a>.
</p><p>Furthermore, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victoria_Louise_of_Prussia" title="Victoria Louise of Prussia">Victoria Louise of Prussia</a>, great-great-great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was a maternal great-grandmother of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Felipe_VI" title="King Felipe VI">King Felipe VI</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Swedish_royalty">Swedish royalty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Swedish royalty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchess_Maria_Pavlovna_of_Russia_(1786%E2%80%931859)" title="Grand Duchess Maria Pavlovna of Russia (1786–1859)">Grand Duchess Maria Pavlovna of Russia</a>, a granddaughter of Catherine, was an ancestor of King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carl_XVI_Gustaf_of_Sweden" title="Carl XVI Gustaf of Sweden">Carl XVI Gustaf of Sweden</a> in two ways, those being the same from Queen <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_II_of_Denmark" title="Margrethe II of Denmark">Margrethe II of Denmark</a>'s maternal ancestry, since the two monarchs are first cousins:
</p>
<ul><li>Her great-great-great-granddaughter, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_of_Baden" title="Victoria of Baden">Victoria of Baden</a>, was a maternal great-grandmother of King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carl_XVI_Gustaf_of_Sweden" title="Carl XVI Gustaf of Sweden">Carl XVI Gustaf of Sweden</a>.</li>
<li>Her great-great-great-granddaughter, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louise_Margaret_of_Prussia" title="Louise Margaret of Prussia">Louise Margaret of Prussia</a>, was a maternal great-grandmother of King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carl_XVI_Gustaf_of_Sweden" title="Carl XVI Gustaf of Sweden">Carl XVI Gustaf of Sweden</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_Greek_royalty">Former Greek royalty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Former Greek royalty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pavlos,_Crown_Prince_of_Greece" title="Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece">Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece</a>, is descended from Catherine the Great in seven ways, three from the same route as the Spanish Royal Family, and four from the same route as the Danish Royal Family:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Olga_Constantinovna_of_Russia" title="Olga Constantinovna of Russia">Olga Constantinovna of Russia</a>, great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was the paternal great-grandmother of <a href="/wiki/Constantine_II_of_Greece" title="Constantine II of Greece">Constantine II of Greece</a>, who is the father of <a href="/wiki/Pavlos,_Crown_Prince_of_Greece" title="Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece">Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sophia_of_Prussia" title="Sophia of Prussia">Sophia of Prussia</a>, great-great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was the paternal grandmother of <a href="/wiki/Constantine_II_of_Greece" title="Constantine II of Greece">Constantine II of Greece</a>, who is the father of <a href="/wiki/Pavlos,_Crown_Prince_of_Greece" title="Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece">Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victoria_Louise_of_Prussia" title="Victoria Louise of Prussia">Victoria Louise of Prussia</a>, great-great-great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was the maternal grandmother of <a href="/wiki/Constantine_II_of_Greece" title="Constantine II of Greece">Constantine II of Greece</a>, who is the father of <a href="/wiki/Pavlos,_Crown_Prince_of_Greece" title="Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece">Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elena_Pavlovna_of_Russia" title="Elena Pavlovna of Russia">Elena Pavlovna of Russia</a>, Grand Duchess of Mecklenburg-Schwerin, and granddaughter of Catherine, was a paternal great-great-great-great-grandmother of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Anne-Marie_of_Greece" title="Queen Anne-Marie of Greece">Queen Anne-Marie of Greece</a>, who is the mother of <a href="/wiki/Pavlos,_Crown_Prince_of_Greece" title="Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece">Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anastasia_Mikhailovna_of_Russia" title="Anastasia Mikhailovna of Russia">Anastasia Mikhailovna of Russia</a>, Grand Duchess of Mecklenburg-Schwerin, and great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was a paternal great-grandmother of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Anne-Marie_of_Greece" title="Queen Anne-Marie of Greece">Queen Anne-Marie of Greece</a>, who is the mother of <a href="/wiki/Pavlos,_Crown_Prince_of_Greece" title="Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece">Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece</a>.</li>
<li>Also, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchess_Maria_Pavlovna_of_Russia_(1786%E2%80%931859)" title="Grand Duchess Maria Pavlovna of Russia (1786–1859)">Grand Duchess Maria Pavlovna of Russia</a>, was a granddaughter of Catherine, and great-great-great-grandmother of <a href="/wiki/Victoria_of_Baden" title="Victoria of Baden">Victoria of Baden</a>, who was a maternal great-grandmother of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Anne-Marie_of_Greece" title="Queen Anne-Marie of Greece">Queen Anne-Marie of Greece</a>, who is the mother of <a href="/wiki/Pavlos,_Crown_Prince_of_Greece" title="Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece">Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece</a>.</li>
<li>Furthermore, the Grand Duchess Maria Pavlovna of Russia was also the great-great-great-grandmother of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louise_Margaret_of_Prussia" title="Louise Margaret of Prussia">Louise Margaret of Prussia</a>, who was another maternal great-grandmother of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Anne-Marie_of_Greece" title="Queen Anne-Marie of Greece">Queen Anne-Marie of Greece</a>, who is the mother of <a href="/wiki/Pavlos,_Crown_Prince_of_Greece" title="Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece">Pavlos, Crown Prince of Greece</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_Italian_royalty">Former Italian royalty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Former Italian royalty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Olga_Constantinovna_of_Russia" title="Olga Constantinovna of Russia">Olga Constantinovna of Russia</a>, great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was the maternal great-grandmother of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Amedeo,_Duke_of_Aosta_(1943%E2%80%932021)" title="Prince Amedeo, Duke of Aosta (1943–2021)">Prince Amedeo of Savoy, Duke of Aosta</a> and his descendants, which include the main branch of the Savoia-Aosta family, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Aimone,_Duke_of_Apulia" title="Prince Aimone, Duke of Apulia">Aimone Duke of Aosta</a>, claimant to the former throne of the Italy.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_Romanian_royalty">Former Romanian royalty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Former Romanian royalty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>King <a href="/wiki/Michael_I_of_Romania" title="Michael I of Romania">Michael I of Romania</a>, was descended from Catherine in three ways:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchess_Maria_Alexandrovna_of_Russia" title="Grand Duchess Maria Alexandrovna of Russia">Grand Duchess Maria Alexandrovna of Russia</a>, great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was the paternal great-grandmother of King <a href="/wiki/Michael_I_of_Romania" title="Michael I of Romania">Michael I of Romania</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Olga_Constantinovna_of_Russia" title="Olga Constantinovna of Russia">Olga Constantinovna of Russia</a>, great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was the maternal great-grandmother of King <a href="/wiki/Michael_I_of_Romania" title="Michael I of Romania">Michael I of Romania</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sophia_of_Prussia" title="Sophia of Prussia">Sophia of Prussia</a>, great-great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was the maternal grandmother of King <a href="/wiki/Michael_I_of_Romania" title="Michael I of Romania">Michael I of Romania</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_Yugoslavian_royalty">Former Yugoslavian royalty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Former Yugoslavian royalty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alexander,_Crown_Prince_of_Yugoslavia" title="Alexander, Crown Prince of Yugoslavia">Alexander, Crown Prince of Yugoslavia</a>, is descended from Catherine in three ways:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchess_Maria_Alexandrovna_of_Russia" title="Grand Duchess Maria Alexandrovna of Russia">Grand Duchess Maria Alexandrovna of Russia</a>, great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was a maternal great-grandmother of King <a href="/wiki/Peter_II_of_Yugoslavia" title="Peter II of Yugoslavia">Peter II of Yugoslavia</a>, who was the father of <a href="/wiki/Alexander,_Crown_Prince_of_Yugoslavia" title="Alexander, Crown Prince of Yugoslavia">Alexander, Crown Prince of Yugoslavia</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Olga_Constantinovna_of_Russia" title="Olga Constantinovna of Russia">Olga Constantinovna of Russia</a>, great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was the maternal great-grandmother of Queen <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_of_Yugoslavia" title="Alexandra of Yugoslavia">Alexandra of Yugoslavia</a>, who was the mother of <a href="/wiki/Alexander,_Crown_Prince_of_Yugoslavia" title="Alexander, Crown Prince of Yugoslavia">Alexander, Crown Prince of Yugoslavia</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sophia_of_Prussia" title="Sophia of Prussia">Sophia of Prussia</a>, great-great-great-granddaughter of Catherine, was the maternal grandmother of Queen <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_of_Yugoslavia" title="Alexandra of Yugoslavia">Alexandra of Yugoslavia</a>, who was the mother of <a href="/wiki/Alexander,_Crown_Prince_of_Yugoslavia" title="Alexander, Crown Prince of Yugoslavia">Alexander, Crown Prince of Yugoslavia</a>.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Title">Title</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Title">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Manifesto of 1763 begins with Catherine's title:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We, Catherine the second, by the Grace of God, Empress and Autocrat of all the Russians at Moscow, Kiev, Vladimir, Novgorod, Tsarina of Kasan, Tsarina of Astrachan, Tsarina of Siberia, Lady of Pleskow and Grand Duchess of Smolensko, Duchess of Estonia and Livland, Carelial, Tver, Yugoria, Permia, Viatka and Bulgaria and others; Lady and Grand Duchess of Novgorod in the Netherland of Chernigov, Resan, Rostov, Yaroslav, Beloosrial, Udoria, Obdoria, Condinia, and Ruler of the entire North region and Lady of the Yurish, of the Cartalinian and Grusinian tsars and the Cabardinian land, of the Cherkessian and Gorsian princes and the lady of the manor and sovereign of many others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[154]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Archives">Archives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Archives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Empress Catherine's correspondence with <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II_Eugene,_Duke_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Frederick II Eugene, Duke of Württemberg">Frederick II Eugene, Duke of Württemberg</a>, (the father of Catherine's daughter-in-law <a href="/wiki/Maria_Feodorovna_(Sophie_Dorothea_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg)" title="Maria Feodorovna (Sophie Dorothea of Württemberg)">Maria Feodorovna</a>) written between 1768 and 1795, is preserved in the State Archive of Stuttgart (Hauptstaatsarchiv Stuttgart) in Stuttgart, Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[155]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>Empress Catherine appears as a character in <a href="/wiki/Lord_Byron" title="Lord Byron">Lord Byron</a>'s unfinished <a href="/wiki/Mock-heroic" title="Mock-heroic">mock-heroic</a> poem <i><a href="/wiki/Don_Juan_(poem)" title="Don Juan (poem)">Don Juan</a></i>.</li>
<li>She was a subject in <a href="/wiki/The_Royal_Diaries" title="The Royal Diaries">The Royal Diaries</a> series in the book <i>Catherine: The Great Journey, Russia, 1743–1745</i> by <a href="/wiki/Kristiana_Gregory" title="Kristiana Gregory">Kristiana Gregory</a>.</li>
<li>The Empress is parodied in Offenbach's operetta <i><a href="/wiki/La_Grande-Duchesse_de_G%C3%A9rolstein" title="La Grande-Duchesse de Gérolstein">La Grande-Duchesse de Gérolstein</a></i> (1867).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corleonis_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Corleonis-160">[156]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ernst_Lubitsch" title="Ernst Lubitsch">Ernst Lubitsch</a>'s silent film <i><a href="/wiki/Forbidden_Paradise" title="Forbidden Paradise">Forbidden Paradise</a></i> (1924) told the story of Catherine's romance with an officer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marlene_Dietrich" title="Marlene Dietrich">Marlene Dietrich</a> portrayed Catherine the Great in the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Scarlet_Empress" title="The Scarlet Empress">The Scarlet Empress</a></i> (1934).</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Rise_of_Catherine_the_Great" title="The Rise of Catherine the Great">The Rise of Catherine the Great</a></i> (1934) is a film starring <a href="/wiki/Elisabeth_Bergner" title="Elisabeth Bergner">Elisabeth Bergner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Fairbanks_Jr." title="Douglas Fairbanks Jr.">Douglas Fairbanks Jr.</a></li>
<li>Lubitsch remade his 1924 silent film as the sound film <i><a href="/wiki/A_Royal_Scandal_(1945_film)" title="A Royal Scandal (1945 film)">A Royal Scandal</a></i> (1945), also known as <i>Czarina</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mae_West" title="Mae West">Mae West</a> published <i><a href="/wiki/Catherine_Was_Great" title="Catherine Was Great">Catherine Was Great</a></i> in 1944, starring in it then and in subsequent productions.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jeanne_Moreau" title="Jeanne Moreau">Jeanne Moreau</a> played a version of Catherine in the farce comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/Great_Catherine_(film)" title="Great Catherine (film)">Great Catherine</a></i> (1968).</li>
<li>The British/Canadian/American TV miniseries <i><a href="/wiki/Young_Catherine" title="Young Catherine">Young Catherine</a></i> (1991), starring <a href="/wiki/Julia_Ormond" title="Julia Ormond">Julia Ormond</a> as Catherine and <a href="/wiki/Vanessa_Redgrave" title="Vanessa Redgrave">Vanessa Redgrave</a> as Empress Elizabeth, is based on Catherine's early life.</li>
<li>The television movie <i><a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great_(1995_film)" title="Catherine the Great (1995 film)">Catherine the Great</a></i> (1995) stars <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Zeta-Jones" title="Catherine Zeta-Jones">Catherine Zeta-Jones</a> as Catherine and Jeanne Moreau as Empress Elizabeth.</li>
<li>Actress <a href="/wiki/Olga_Antonova_(actress)" title="Olga Antonova (actress)">Olga Antonova</a>   played the role of the Empress in the 2000 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Captain%27s_Daughter_(2000_film)" title="The Captain's Daughter (2000 film)">The Captain's Daughter</a></i>, based on the novel of the same name by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Pushkin" title="Alexander Pushkin">Alexander Pushkin</a>.</li>
<li>Her rise to power and reign are portrayed in the award-winning <a href="/wiki/Russia-1" title="Russia-1">Russia-1</a> television series <a href="/wiki/Ekaterina_(TV_series)" title="Ekaterina (TV series)"><i>Ekaterina</i></a>, which has been extended for a second season in 2017 and a third season in 2019.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Channel_One_Russia" title="Channel One Russia">Channel One Russia</a> television series <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great_(TV_series)" title="Catherine the Great (TV series)">Catherine the Great</a></i> was released in 2015.</li>
<li>Catherine (portrayed by Meghan Tonjes) is featured in the web series <i><a href="/wiki/Epic_Rap_Battles_of_History#History" title="Epic Rap Battles of History">Epic Rap Battles of History</a></i>, in the episode "Alexander the Great vs. Ivan the Terrible" (12 July 2016), pitted against the titular characters, as well as <a href="/wiki/Frederick_the_Great" title="Frederick the Great">Frederick the Great</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pompey_the_Great" title="Pompey the Great">Pompey the Great</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[157]</a></sup></li>
<li>The television miniseries <i><a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great_(miniseries)" title="Catherine the Great (miniseries)">Catherine the Great</a></i> (2019) stars <a href="/wiki/Helen_Mirren" title="Helen Mirren">Helen Mirren</a>.</li>
<li>She is portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Elle_Fanning" title="Elle Fanning">Elle Fanning</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Hulu" title="Hulu">Hulu</a> television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_(TV_series)" title="The Great (TV series)">The Great</a></i> (2020).</li>
<li>She appears as a leader of the Russian civilization in <a href="/wiki/Civilization_(series)" title="Civilization (series)"><i>Civilization</i></a> games <a href="/wiki/Civilization_II" title="Civilization II"><i>II</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Civilization_III" title="Civilization III"><i>III</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Civilization_IV" title="Civilization IV"><i>IV</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Civilization_V" title="Civilization V"><i>V</i></a>.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">Ancestry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Ancestry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_prominent_Catherinians">List of prominent Catherinians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: List of prominent Catherinians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monument_to_Catherine_II_in_SPB.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2451" data-file-width="3700" decoding="async" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Monument_to_Catherine_II_in_SPB.jpg/300px-Monument_to_Catherine_II_in_SPB.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Monument_to_Catherine_II_in_SPB.jpg/450px-Monument_to_Catherine_II_in_SPB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Monument_to_Catherine_II_in_SPB.jpg/600px-Monument_to_Catherine_II_in_SPB.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monument_to_Catherine_II_in_SPB.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Monument to Catherine the Great in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>, surrounded by prominent persons of her era</div></div></div>
<p>Pre-eminent figures in Catherinian Russia include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ivan_Betskoy" title="Ivan Betskoy">Ivan Betskoy</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Bezborodko" title="Alexander Bezborodko">Alexander Bezborodko</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yakov_Bulgakov" title="Yakov Bulgakov">Yakov Bulgakov</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gavrila_Derzhavin" title="Gavrila Derzhavin">Gavrila Derzhavin</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Jones" title="John Paul Jones">John Paul Jones</a> – the American sea captain and admiral served under Catherine in naval actions against the Turks in the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> in 1788.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Kheraskov" title="Mikhail Kheraskov">Mikhail Kheraskov</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Levitzky" title="Dmitry Levitzky">Dmitry Levitsky</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alexei_Grigoryevich_Orlov" title="Alexei Grigoryevich Orlov">Aleksey Orlov</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikita_Ivanovich_Panin" title="Nikita Ivanovich Panin">Nikita Panin</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grigory_Potyomkin" title="Grigory Potyomkin">Grigory Potemkin</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicholas_Repnin" title="Nicholas Repnin">Nicholas Repnin</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Rumyantsev" title="Pyotr Rumyantsev">Peter Rumyantsev</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Shcherbatov" title="Mikhail Shcherbatov">Mikhailo Shcherbatov</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Suvorov" title="Alexander Suvorov">Alexander Suvorov</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fyodor_Fyodorovich_Ushakov" title="Fyodor Fyodorovich Ushakov">Fyodor Ushakov</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yekaterina_Romanovna_Vorontsova-Dashkova" title="Yekaterina Romanovna Vorontsova-Dashkova">Catherine Vorontsova</a></li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Explanatory_notes">Explanatory notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catherine_the_Great&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Explanatory notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
